href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a></dd></dl>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Group of Seven</b> (<b>G7</b>) is a group consisting of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. These countries, with the seven largest advanced economies in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> represent more than 62% of the <a href="/wiki/National_wealth" class="mw-redirect" title="National wealth">global net wealth</a> ($280&#160;trillion).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-credit-suisse1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-credit-suisse1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The G7 countries also represent more than 46% of the global <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) based on <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal values</a>, and more than 32% of the global GDP based on <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is also represented at the G7 summit.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" tocsection-15"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G7_flags,_Toronto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg/220px-G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg/330px-G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg/440px-G7_flags%2C_Toronto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2721" data-file-height="2005" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G7_flags,_Toronto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flags of G7 members as seen on <a href="/wiki/University_Avenue_(Toronto)" title="University Avenue (Toronto)">University Avenue (Toronto)</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/220px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/330px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg/440px-G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3861" data-file-height="2574" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G7_in_het_Catshuis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>G7 leaders during the 2014 emergency meeting about the Russian annexation of Crimea, hosted by the Netherlands.</div></div></div>\n<p>The concept of a forum for the world\'s major industrialized countries emerged before the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>. On Sunday, 25 March 1973, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">U.S. Secretary of the Treasury</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_P._Shultz" title="George P. Shultz">George Shultz</a>, convened an informal gathering of <a href="/wiki/Finance_ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="Finance ministers">finance ministers</a> from West Germany <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Schmidt" title="Helmut Schmidt">Helmut Schmidt</a>, France <a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9ry_Giscard_d%27Estaing" title="Val\xc3\xa9ry Giscard d&#39;Estaing">Val\xc3\xa9ry Giscard d\'Estaing</a>, and the United Kingdom <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Barber" title="Anthony Barber">Anthony Barber</a> before an upcoming meeting in Washington, D.C. When running the idea past President <a href="/wiki/Richard_M._Nixon" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard M. Nixon">Nixon</a>, he noted that he would be out of town and offered use of <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">the White House</a>. The meeting was subsequently held in the <a href="/wiki/Library_(White_House)" title="Library (White House)">library</a> on the ground floor.<sup id="cite_ref-Schultz_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schultz-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Taking their name from the setting, this original group of four became known as the "Library Group".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In mid-1973, at the World Bank-IMF meetings, Shultz proposed the addition of Japan to the original four nations, who agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-Schultz_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schultz-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The informal gathering of senior financial officials from the United States, the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>, Japan, and France became known as the "Group of Five".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Then, in 1974, <a href="/wiki/Georges_Pompidou" title="Georges Pompidou">President Pompidou</a> of France died and his immediate successor refused to run in the special election, making three heads of state in one year. Chancellor Brandt of West Germany was forced to resign in a scandal, and his successor lasted only nine days, making three heads of government in one year. Then <a href="/wiki/President_Nixon" class="mw-redirect" title="President Nixon">President Nixon</a> of the United States and <a href="/wiki/Kakuei_Tanaka" title="Kakuei Tanaka">Prime Minister Tanaka</a> of Japan were forced to resign in disgrace. <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> was forced to broker a deal to form a government after a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_February_1974" title="United Kingdom general election, February 1974">hung election</a>, which was so unstable that <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_October_1974" title="United Kingdom general election, October 1974">another election the same year</a> had to take place, and finally, the traditionally unstable government of 1st Italian Republic changed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Italy" title="List of Prime Ministers of Italy">Prime Ministers</a> yet again. American President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, who had been a mere Congressman a year before, asked some other new heads of state/government to hold a retreat the following year to get to know one another. \n</p><p>So, in <a href="/wiki/1st_G6_summit" title="1st G6 summit">1975, a summit</a> hosted by France brought together representatives of six governments: France, West Germany, Italy, Japan, the United Kingdom, and the United States. Schmidt and Giscard d\'Estaing were heads of government in their respective countries, and since they both spoke fluent English, it occurred to them that they, and British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> and U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> could get together in an informal retreat and discuss election results and the issues of the day. In late spring, d\'Estaing of France invited the <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Heads of government">heads of government</a> from West Germany, Italy, Japan, the United Kingdom, and the United States to a summit in <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Rambouillet" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau de Rambouillet">Ch\xc3\xa2teau de Rambouillet</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-evian_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evian-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the annual meeting of the six leaders was organized under a rotating presidency, forming the Group of Six (G6). In 1976, with Wilson out as prime minister of Britain, Schmidt and <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> felt an English speaker with more experience was needed, so Canada\'s <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a> was invited to join the group<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and the group became the Group of Seven (<a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-evian_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evian-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Since first invited by the United Kingdom in 1977 the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has been represented by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">president of the European Commission</a>, and the leader of the country that holds the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">presidency of the Council of the European Union</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">Council President</a> now also regularly attends.\n</p><p>Until the 1985 <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Accord" title="Plaza Accord">Plaza Accord</a> no one outside a tight official circle knew when the seven finance ministers met and what they agreed. The summit was announced the day before and a communiqu\xc3\xa9 was issued afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following <a href="/wiki/20th_G7_summit" title="20th G7 summit">1994\'s G7 summit in Naples</a>, Russian officials held separate meetings with leaders of the G7 after the group\'s summits. This informal arrangement was dubbed the Political 8 (P8) \xe2\x80\x93 or, colloquially, the G7+1. At the invitation of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> and President of the United States <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Russian President <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> was invited first as a guest observer, later as a full participant. After the 1997 meeting Russia was formally invited to the next meeting and formally joined the group in 1998, resulting in a new governmental political forum, the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Eight" title="Group of Eight">Group of Eight</a> or G8.<sup id="cite_ref-evian_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evian-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The Russian Federation, in fact, had and has limited net <a href="/wiki/National_wealth" class="mw-redirect" title="National wealth">national wealth</a> and financial weight compared to the other members of the G8. Russia also has never been a major advanced economy according to the IMF.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However, the Russian Federation was ejected from the G8 political forum in March 2014 following the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Russian annexation of Crimea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_function">Early function</span></h2>\n<p>The organization was founded to facilitate shared macroeconomic initiatives by its members in response to the collapse of the exchange rate 1971, during the time of the <a href="/wiki/Nixon_shock" title="Nixon shock">Nixon shock</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1970s_energy_crisis" title="1970s energy crisis">1970s energy crisis</a> and the ensuing recession.<sup id="cite_ref-Bayne_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayne-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Work">Work</span></h2>\n<div class="noviewer thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px"><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right"><div style="font-size:80%;"><a href="/wiki/5th_G7_summit" title="5th G7 summit">5th</a>, <a href="/wiki/12th_G7_summit" title="12th G7 summit">12th</a>, <a href="/wiki/19th_G7_summit" title="19th G7 summit">19th</a></div></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:81.797%;left:83.519%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="26th" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/8px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png" title="26th" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/12px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/16px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="12" data-file-height="12" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:5px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><div style="font-size:80%;"><a href="/wiki/26th_G8_summit" title="26th G8 summit">26th</a></div></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:20.888%;left:59.553%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="34th" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/8px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png" title="34th" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/12px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/16px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="12" data-file-height="12" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:5px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><div style="font-size:80%;"><a href="/wiki/34th_G8_summit" title="34th G8 summit">34th</a></div></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:72.802%;left:40.845%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="42nd" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/8px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png" title="42nd" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/12px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Arrows_12x12_w.svg/16px-Arrows_12x12_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="12" data-file-height="12" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:5px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left"><div style="font-size:80%;"><a href="/wiki/42nd_G7_summit" title="42nd G7 summit">42nd</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japan_location_map_with_side_map_of_the_Ryukyu_Islands.svg" title="File:Japan location map with side map of the Ryukyu Islands.svg"> </a></div>Host venues of G7 summits in Japan.</div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1975, the group meets annually on summit site to discuss economic policies; since 1987, the G7 Finance Ministers have met at least semi-annually, up to 4 times a year at stand-alone meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-meet_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meet-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1996, the G7 launched an initiative for the 42 <a href="/wiki/Heavily_indebted_poor_countries" title="Heavily indebted poor countries">heavily indebted poor countries</a> (HIPC).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, the G7 decided to get more directly involved in "managing the international monetary system" through the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Stability_Forum" title="Financial Stability Forum">Financial Stability Forum</a>, formed earlier in 1999 and the G-20, established following the summit, to "promote dialogue between major industrial and emerging market countries".<sup id="cite_ref-Van_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Van-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The G7 also announced their plan to cancel 90% of bilateral, and multilateral debt for the HIPC, totaling $100 billion. In 2005 the G7 announced debt reductions of "up to 100%" to be negotiated on a "case by case" basis.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008 the G7 met twice in Washington, D.C. to discuss the global <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and in February 2009 in Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The group of finance ministers pledged to take "all necessary steps" to stem the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-O&#39;Grady_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O&#39;Grady-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 March 2014, the G7 condemned the "Russian Federation\'s violation of the sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-toro_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toro-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The G7 stated "that the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) remains the institution best prepared to help Ukraine address its immediate economic challenges through policy advice and financing, conditioned on needed reforms", and that the G7 was "committed to mobilize rapid technical assistance to support Ukraine in addressing its macroeconomic, regulatory and anti-corruption challenges."<sup id="cite_ref-toro_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toro-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 24 March 2014, the G7 convened an emergency meeting in response to the Russian Federation\'s <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> at the official residence of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prime Minister of the Netherlands">Prime Minister of the Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catshuis" title="Catshuis">Catshuis</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. This location was chosen because all G7 leaders were already present to attend the <a href="/wiki/2014_Nuclear_Security_Summit" title="2014 Nuclear Security Summit">2014 Nuclear Security Summit</a> hosted by the Netherlands. This was the first G7 meeting neither taking place in a member nation nor having the host leader participating in the meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On 4 June 2014 leaders at the G7 summit in Brussels, condemned Moscow for its "continuing violation" of Ukraine\'s sovereignty, in their joint statement and stated they were prepared to impose further sanctions on Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc201406_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc201406-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This meeting was the first since Russia was expelled from the G8 following its annexation of Crimea in March.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc201406_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc201406-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The annual G7 leaders summit is attended by the heads of government.<sup id="cite_ref-feldman1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feldman1-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The member country holding the G7 presidency is responsible for organizing and hosting the year\'s summit. The serial annual summits can be parsed chronologically in arguably distinct ways, including as the sequence of host countries for the summits has recurred over time and series.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Generally every country hosts the summit once every 7 years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_summits">List of summits</span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th></th>\n<th Until the <a href="/wiki/38th_G8_summit" title="38th G8 summit">38th G8 summit</a> in 2012, it has been invited to the Summit annually without interruption. Also, with permission from a G8 leader, other nations were invited to the Summit on a periodical basis for the first time. Nigeria, Algeria and Senegal accepted their invitations here. The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> was also invited for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-G8_paper_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G8_paper-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/27th_G8_summit" title="27th G8 summit">27th</a></td>\n<td>21\xe2\x80\x9322 July 2001</td>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>Leaders from Bangladesh, Mali and El Salvador accepted their invitations here.<sup id="cite_ref-G8_paper_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G8_paper-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Demonstrator <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Giuliani" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlo Giuliani">Carlo Giuliani</a> is shot and killed by police during a violent demonstration. The G7 also issued a warning on the United Kingdom that "a UK exit from the EU would reverse the trend towards greater global trade and investment, and the jobs they create and is a further serious risk to growth".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Commitment to an EU\xe2\x80\x93Japan Free Trade Agreement.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/43rd_G7_summit" title="43rd G7 summit">43rd</a></td>\n<td>26\xe2\x80\x9327 May 2017<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Taormina" title="Taormina">Taormina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.g7italy.it/en">[4]</a></small></td>\n<td>G7 leaders emphasized common endeavours: to end the Syrian crisis, to fulfill the UN mission in Libya and reducing the presence of ISIS, ISIL and Da\'esh in Syria and Iraq. North Korea was urged to comply with UN resolutions, Russian responsibility was stressed for Ukrainian conflict. Supporting economic activity and ensuring price stability was demanded while inequalities in trade and gender were called to be challenged. It was agreed to help countries in creating conditions that address the drivers of migration: ending hunger, increasing competitiveness and advancing global health security.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/44th_G7_summit" title="44th G7 summit">44th</a></td>\n<td>8\xe2\x80\x939 June 2018</td>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a><sup id="cite_ref-gcnews_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcnews-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/La_Malbaie" title="La Malbaie">La Malbaie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a></td>\n<td><small><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://g7.gc.ca/">[5]</a></small></td>\n<td>It took place at the Manoir Richelieu. Prime Minister Trudeau announced five themes for Canada\xe2\x80\x99s G7 presidency which began in January 2018. Climate, along with commerce trades, was one of the main themes. \xe2\x80\x9c<i>Working together on climate change, oceans and clean energy</i>\xe2\x80\x9d <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The G7 members\' final statement contains 28 points. US President Donald Trump didn\'t agree to the economic section of the final statement.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The G7 members also announced to recall sanctions and to be ready to take further restrictive measures against Russian Federation for the failure of Minsk Agreement\'s complete implementation.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/45th_G7_summit" title="45th G7 summit">45th</a></td>\n<td>TBD, 2019</td>\n<td><span title="France">France</a><sup id="cite_ref-presidency_rotation_2015-2020_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidency_rotation_2015-2020-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><a background:#98fb98;"><img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">Advanced\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="nowrap">European Union</span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">4,485,000\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">18,527,116\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">18,640,411\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">36,645\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">36,869\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">0.865\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: right;">505,570,700\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;" data-sort-value="" class="table-na">N/A\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center; background:#98fb98;"><img alt="Green tick" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/13px-Green_check.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/20px-Green_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Green_check.svg/26px-Green_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span>\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;" data-sort-value="" class="table-na">N/A\n</td>\n<td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;" data-sort-value="" class="table-na">N/A\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The G7 is composed of the seven <a href="/wiki/National_wealth" class="mw-redirect" title="National wealth">wealthiest</a> advanced countries. The <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People\'s Republic of China</a>, according to its data, would be the second-largest with the 10.3% of the world net wealth,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> but is excluded because the IMF and other main global institutions do not consider China an advanced country and because of its relatively low net wealth per adult and HDI. <sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017 <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Suisse" class="mw-redirect" title="Cr\xc3\xa9dit Suisse">Cr\xc3\xa9dit Suisse</a> reports the G7 (without the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>) represents above 62% of the global <a href="/wiki/Net_worth" title="Net worth">net wealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-credit-suisse1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-credit-suisse1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Including the EU the G7 represents over 70% of the global net wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_facts">Member facts</span></h3>\n<ul><li>7 of the 7 top-ranked <a href="/wiki/Advanced_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced economies">advanced economies</a> with the current largest GDP and with the highest <a href="/wiki/National_wealth" class="mw-redirect" title="National wealth">national wealth</a> (United States, Japan, Germany, UK, France, Italy, Canada).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>7 of the 15 top-ranked countries with the highest net wealth per capita (United States, France, Japan, United Kingdom, Italy, Canada, Germany).</li>\n<li>7 of 10 top-ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">leading export countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>5 of 10 top-ranked countries with the largest <a href="/wiki/Gold_reserve#Officially_reported_gold_holdings" title="Gold reserve">gold reserves</a> (United States, Germany, Italy, France, Japan).</li>\n<li>7 of 10 top-ranked economies (by <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">nominal GDP</a>), according to latest (2016 data) International Monetary Fund\'s statistics.</li>\n<li>5 countries with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal GDP per capita</a> above US$40,000 (United States, Canada, Germany, United Kingdom, France).</li>\n<li>4 countries with a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund" title="Sovereign wealth fund">sovereign wealth fund</a>, administered by either a national or a state/provincial government (United States, France, Canada, Italy).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>7 of 30 top-ranked nations with large amounts of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_foreign-exchange_reserves" title="List of countries by foreign-exchange reserves">foreign-exchange reserves</a> in their <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central banks</a>.</li>\n<li>3 out of 9 <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons" title="List of states with nuclear weapons">countries having nuclear weapons</a> (France, UK, United States),<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> plus 2 countries that have <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_sharing" title="Nuclear sharing">nuclear weapon sharing programs</a> (Germany, Italy).<sup id="cite_ref-RUSI-2010_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RUSI-2010-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>6 of the 9 largest <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_by_country#Nuclear_power_output_in_megawatts" title="Nuclear power by country">nuclear energy producers</a> (United States, France, Japan, Germany, Canada, UK), although Germany announced in 2011 that it will close all of its nuclear power plants by 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 T\xc5\x8dhoku earthquake and tsunami">2011 T\xc5\x8dhoku earthquake and tsunami</a>, Japan shut down all of its nuclear reactors.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> However, Japan restarted several nuclear reactors, with the refueling of other reactors underway.</li>\n<li>7 of the 10 top donors to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_funding" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations funding">UN budget</a> for the 2016 annual fiscal year.</li>\n<li>5 countries with a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index#2016_report" title="Human Development Index">HDI index for 2016 of 0.9 and higher</a> (United States, Germany, United Kingdom, Canada, Japan).</li>\n<li>2 countries with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_credit_rating" title="List of countries by credit rating">highest credit rating</a> from <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitch_Ratings" title="Fitch Ratings">Fitch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody&#39;s Investors Service">Moody\'s</a> at the same time (Canada and Germany).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>3 countries are <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchies</a> (United Kingdom, Canada, Japan), 2 are <a href="/wiki/Presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential republic">presidential republics</a> (France, United States) and the other 2 are <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republics</a> (Germany and Italy).</li>\n<li>1 country (Canada) has legalized cannabis consumption at the federal level, to take effect October 17, 2018. Canada is the first G7 country to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_suspension_and_following_exclusion_of_Russian_Federation">2014 suspension and following exclusion of Russian Federation</span></h3>\n<p>In March 2014 Russian Federation was suspended by G7 members from the political forum G8 following the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a>. After the suspension, on January 2017 Russian Federation decided permanently to leave the G8. It was confirmed in June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN.com_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN.com-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-russia-suspension_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russia-suspension-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_protests">2015 protests</span></h3>\n<p>In 2015, despite Germany\'s immense efforts to prevent it and despite the remote location of the summit, the luxury hotel Schloss Elmau at the foot of the Wetterstein mountains at an altitude of 1,008&#160;m (3,307&#160;ft) above sea level, about 300 of the 7500 protesters led by the group \'Stop-G7\' managed to reach the 3 m high and 7&#160;km long security fence surrounding the summit location. The protesters questioned the legitimacy of the G7 to make decisions that could affect the whole world. Authorities had banned demonstrations in the closer area of the summit location and 20,000 policemen were on duty in Southern Bavaria to keep activists and protesters from interfering with the summit.<sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel07June_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel07June-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bild03June_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bild03June-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_Trump_conflict_over_tariffs_and_Russian_Federation">2018 Trump conflict over tariffs and Russian Federation</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/44th_G7_summit" title="44th G7 summit">2018 meeting in Charlevoix, Canada</a>, was marred by fractious negotiations concerning tariffs and Donald Trump\'s unorthodox position that Russia should be reinstated to the political forum G8, despite its limited national wealth and its lack of an advanced economy according to the IMF. The Trump administration had just imposed steel and aluminum tariffs on many countries, including European countries that are fellow members of the G7, and Canada, the host country for the 2018 meeting. Trump arrived late, left the meeting early, expressed dismay at Canadian Prime Minister Trudeau for holding a press conference in which Canada restated its position on tariffs, and directed his representatives at the meeting to not sign the economic section of the joint communique that is typically issued at the conclusion of the meeting. An opinion writer at the <i>Washington Post</i>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Boot" title="Max Boot">Max Boot</a>, opined that Trump had turned the meeting into a confrontation between the "G-6 versus the G-1."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and economist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Krugman" title="Paul Krugman">Paul Krugman</a> noted that it probably had more to do with whatever hold Putin has over Trump personally.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> German Chancellor Angela Merkel described Trump\'s behavior as a "depressing withdrawal," while French President Emmanuel Macron invited him "to be serious."<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In the final statement signed by all members except the USA, G7 announced its intention to recall sanctions and to be ready to take further restrictive measures within the next months against the Russian Federation for its failure to completely implement the <a href="/wiki/Minsk_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Minsk Agreement">Minsk Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<ul><li><a
